 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Item&nbsp;2.02.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Results of Operations and Financial Condition. </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On October&nbsp;29, 2018, we issued a press release announcing earnings for the third quarter ended September&nbsp;30, 2018. A copy of the earnings press
release is furnished as Exhibit 99.1 to this current report. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The information in this Item 2.02, including Exhibit 99.1, will not be deemed
&#147;filed&#148; for purposes of Section&nbsp;18 of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (the &#147;Exchange Act&#148;), or otherwise subject to the liabilities under that section and it will not be incorporated by reference in any
filing under the Securities Act of 1933, as amended, or the Exchange Act, except as expressly set forth by specific reference in such a filing. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Item&nbsp;5.02.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Departure of Directors or Certain Officers; Election of Directors; Appointment of Certain Officers; Compensatory
Arrangements of Certain Officers. </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On October&nbsp;29, 2018, we announced that Hubert Weber, EVP and President, Europe, will retire on
January&nbsp;31, 2019 and will be succeeded by Vinzenz Gruber, currently President, Western Europe, as EVP and President, Europe. </P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Net revenues declined 3.7% driven by currency; Organic Net
Revenue<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> grew 1.2%, which includes 60 basis points of headwinds for malware effects in the prior year </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Operating income margin was 11.7%, down 620 basis points; Adjusted Operating Income<SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> margin was 17.1%, up 40 basis points </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

</P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">DEERFIELD, Ill. &#150; October&nbsp;29, 2018 &#150; Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) today reported its
third quarter 2018 results. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We performed well in the third quarter,&#148; said Dirk Van de Put, Chairman and CEO.&nbsp;&#147;We
continue to see good momentum in emerging markets, underpinned by solid volume growth and strong execution. We are beginning to deliver against our new long-term growth strategy by implementing a more agile innovation model and establishing a new
commercial structure that will improve our consumer focus and drive greater local accountability, while igniting our global and local brand and innovation agendas.&#148; </P>

<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><U>Third Quarter Commentary </U></I></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Net revenues</B> declined 3.7&nbsp;percent, driven by the impact of currency. Organic Net Revenue increased
1.2&nbsp;percent, partially tempered by lapping last year&#146;s malware recovery benefit. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Gross profit margin</B> was 38.4&nbsp;percent, down 60 basis points driven primarily by an unfavorable impact
from currency and commodity hedging activities. Adjusted Gross Profit margin was 40.6&nbsp;percent, an increase of 110 basis points, driven by higher pricing and productivity savings. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Operating income margin</B> was 11.7&nbsp;percent, down 620 basis points, due to the prior-year gain on a
divestiture and the prior-year benefit of an indirect tax matter, as well as unfavorable current year impacts from currency and commodity hedging activities. These items were partially offset by lower restructuring program costs and the lapping of
prior year malware-related expenses. Adjusted Operating Income margin increased 40 basis points to 17.1&nbsp;percent due to pricing and productivity savings partially offset by other income and expense items. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Diluted EPS</B> was $0.81, up 27&nbsp;percent, driven by the gain on equity method investment transaction
partially offset by the unfavorable impact from currency and commodity hedging activities and the lapping of the prior-year gain on divestitures and the prior-year benefit from the resolution of indirect tax matters. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Adjusted EPS</B> was $0.62 and grew 18&nbsp;percent on a constant-currency basis, driven primarily by
favorability in taxes, operating gains and fewer shares outstanding. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Capital Return</B>: The company returned approximately $800&nbsp;million to shareholders in common stock
repurchases and cash dividends. Year to date, the company has returned approximately $2.6&nbsp;billion to shareholders. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>2018 Outlook
</B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International provides guidance on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> basis, as the company cannot
predict some elements that are included in reported GAAP results, including the impact of foreign exchange. Refer to the Outlook section in the discussion of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures below for more details.
The company now expects full year 2018 Organic Net Revenue growth to be approximately 2&nbsp;percent. The company maintains its outlook for Adjusted Operating Income margin of approximately 17&nbsp;percent and double-digit Adjusted EPS growth on a
constant-currency basis. The company estimates currency translation would decrease net revenue growth by approximately 1 percent<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">3</SUP> with a negative $0.02 impact to Adjusted EPS<SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">3</SUP>. In addition, the company continues to expect Free Cash Flow<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> of approximately $2.8&nbsp;billion. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Leadership Change </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Vinzenz Gruber</B>, currently President, Western Europe, will become EVP and President, Europe, succeeding <B>Hubert Weber</B>, EVP and
President, Europe upon his retirement on January&nbsp;31, 2019. Gruber brings extensive marketing and commercial experience, both at Mondel&#275;z International and other leading consumer goods companies. Weber is retiring after 29 years of service
with the company. Weber has led the European business since 2013, navigating a period of significant transformation and delivering strong business results and creating a robust platform for future growth. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Conference Call </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z
International will host a conference call for investors with accompanying slides to review its results at 5 p.m. ET today. A listen-only webcast will be provided at <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U>. An archive of the webcast will be available on
the company&#146;s web site. The company will be live tweeting the event at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About Mondel&#275;z International </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) empowers people to snack right in approximately 160 countries around the world. With 2017 net
revenues of approximately $26&nbsp;billion, MDLZ is leading the future of snacking with iconic global and local brands such as <I>Oreo</I>, <I>belVita</I> and <I>LU</I> biscuits; <I>Cadbury Dairy Milk</I>, <I>Milka</I> and <I>Toblerone</I>
chocolate; <I>Sour Patch Kids</I> candy and <I>Trident</I> gum. Mondel&#275;z International is a proud member of the Standard and Poor&#146;s 500, Nasdaq 100 and Dow Jones Sustainability Index. Visit <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U> or follow
the company on Twitter at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>End Notes </B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="4%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">1.</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Organic Net Revenue, Adjusted Operating Income (and Adjusted Operating Income margin), Adjusted EPS, Adjusted

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Additional Definitions </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Emerging markets consist of the Latin America region in its entirety; the Asia, Middle East and Africa region excluding Australia, New Zealand
and Japan; and the following countries from the Europe region: Russia, Ukraine, Turkey, Kazakhstan, Belarus, Georgia, Poland, Czech Republic, Slovak Republic, Hungary, Bulgaria, Romania, the Baltics and the East Adriatic countries. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Developed markets include the entire North America region, the Europe region excluding the countries included in the emerging markets
definition, and Australia, New Zealand and Japan from the Asia, Middle East and Africa region. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Forward-Looking Statements </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This press release contains a number of forward-looking statements. Words, and variations of words, such as &#147;will,&#148;
&#147;expect,&#148; &#147;may,&#148; &#147;would,&#148; &#147;could,&#148; &#147;deliver,&#148; &#147;estimate,&#148; &#147;anticipate,&#148; &#147;guidance,&#148; &#147;outlook&#148; and similar expressions are intended to identify the
company&#146;s forward-looking statements, including, but not limited to, statements about: the company&#146;s future performance, including its future revenue growth, earnings per share, margins and cash flow; currency and the effect of foreign
exchange translation on the company&#146;s results of operations; the company&#146;s accounting for and the impact of U.S. tax reform; the company&#146;s liability related to partial withdrawal from the Bakery and Confectionery Union and Industry
International Pension Fund and timing of receipt of the assessment from the Fund; the Brazilian indirect tax matter; the impacts of the malware incident; the company&#146;s growth strategy and its effects on the company&#146;s business; and the
company&#146;s outlook, including 2018 Organic Net Revenue growth, Adjusted Operating Income margin, Adjusted EPS and Free Cash Flow. These forward-looking statements are subject to a number of risks and uncertainties, many of which are beyond the
company&#146;s control, which could cause the company&#146;s actual results to differ materially from those indicated in the company&#146;s forward-looking statements. Such factors include, but are not limited to, risks from operating globally
including in emerging markets; changes in currency exchange rates, controls and restrictions; continued volatility of commodity and other input costs; weakness in economic conditions; weakness in consumer spending; pricing actions; tax matters
including changes in tax rates and laws, disagreements with taxing authorities and imposition of new taxes; use of information technology and third party service providers; unanticipated disruptions to the company&#146;s business, such as the
malware incident, cyberattacks or other security breaches; competition; the restructuring program and the company&#146;s other transformation initiatives not yielding the anticipated benefits; and changes in the assumptions on which the
restructuring program is based. Please also see the company&#146;s risk factors, as they may be amended from time to time, set forth in its filings with the SEC, including the company&#146;s most recently filed Annual Report on Form <FONT

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:14pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. and Subsidiaries </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:12pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Reconciliation of GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Financial Measures </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:12pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>(Unaudited) </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company reports its
financial results in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States (&#147;GAAP&#148;). However, management believes that also presenting certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
provides additional information to facilitate comparison of the company&#146;s historical operating results and trends in its underlying operating results, and provides additional transparency on how the company evaluates its business. Management
uses these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures in making financial, operating and planning decisions and in evaluating the company&#146;s performance. The company also believes that presenting these measures allows
investors to view its performance using the same measures that the company uses in evaluating its financial and business performance and trends. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
company considers quantitative and qualitative factors in assessing whether to adjust for the impact of items that may be significant or that could affect an understanding of its ongoing financial and business performance and trends. The adjustments
generally fall within the following categories: acquisition&nbsp;&amp; divestiture activities, gains and losses on intangible asset sales and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairments, major program restructuring activities,
constant currency and related adjustments, major program financing and hedging activities and other major items affecting comparability of operating results. See below for a description of adjustments to the company&#146;s U.S. GAAP financial
measures included herein. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> information should be considered as supplemental in nature and is not meant to
be considered in isolation or as a substitute for the related financial information prepared in accordance with U.S. GAAP. In addition, the company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures may not be the same as or
comparable to similar <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures presented by other companies. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Because GAAP financial measures on a
forward-looking basis are not accessible and reconciling information is not available without unreasonable effort, the company has not provided that information with regard to the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
in the company&#146;s outlook. Refer to the Outlook section below for more details. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DEFINITIONS OF THE COMPANY&#146;S <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> FINANCIAL MEASURES </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures and corresponding metrics reflect how the company evaluates its
operating results currently and provide improved comparability of operating results. As new events or circumstances arise, these definitions could change. When these definitions change, the company provides the updated definitions and presents the
related <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> historical results on a comparable basis. When items no longer impact the company&#146;s current or future presentation of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> operating results,
the company removes these items from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> definitions. During the third quarter of 2018, as the company began to apply highly inflationary accounting for Argentina, the company excluded the
remeasurement gains or losses related to remeasuring net monetary assets or liabilities in Argentina during the period to be consistent with the company&#146;s prior accounting for these remeasurement gains/losses for Venezuela when it was subject
to highly inflationary accounting prior to 2016. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Organic Net Revenue&#148;</B> is defined as net revenues excluding the impacts of acquisitions;
divestitures; and currency rate fluctuations. The company also evaluates Organic Net Revenue growth from emerging markets and its Power Brands. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted Gross Profit&#148;</B> is defined as gross profit excluding the Simplify to Grow Program;
acquisition integration costs; the operating results of divestitures; <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative contracts; and
incremental expenses related to the 2017 malware incident. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Gross Profit margin,&#148; which is subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Gross Profit. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s
Adjusted Gross Profit on a constant currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted Operating Income&#148;</B> and <B>&#147;Adjusted Segment Operating Income&#148;</B> are defined
as operating income (or segment operating income) excluding the impacts of the items listed in the Adjusted Gross Profit definition as well as gains or losses (including <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairment charges) on
goodwill and intangible assets; divestiture or acquisition gains or losses and related divestiture, acquisition and integration costs; remeasurement of net monetary position; impacts from resolution of tax matters; CEO transition remuneration; and
impact from pension participation changes. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Operating Income margin&#148; and &#147;Adjusted Segment Operating Income margin&#148;, which are subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Operating Income and
Adjusted Segment Operating Income. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Operating Income and Adjusted Segment Operating Income on a constant currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted EPS&#148;</B> is defined as diluted EPS attributable to Mondel&#275;z International from
continuing operations excluding the impacts of the items listed in the Adjusted Operating Income definition as well as losses on debt extinguishment and related expenses; gain on equity method investment transactions; net earnings from divestitures;
gains or losses on interest rate swaps no longer designated as accounting cash flow hedges due to changed financing and hedging plans; and U.S. tax reform discrete impacts. Similarly, within Adjusted EPS, the company&#146;s equity method investment
net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its investees&#146; unusual or infrequent items. The tax impact of each of the items excluded from the company&#146;s GAAP results was computed based on the facts and tax assumptions associated with
each item and such impacts have also been excluded from Adjusted EPS. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted EPS on a constant currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Free Cash Flow&#148;</B> is defined as net cash provided by operating activities less capital
expenditures. Free Cash Flow is the company&#146;s primary measure used to monitor its cash flow performance. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">See the attached
schedules for supplemental financial data and corresponding reconciliations of the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures referred to above to the most comparable GAAP financial measures for the three months and nine
months ended September&nbsp;30, 2018. See Items Impacting Comparability of Operating Results below for more information about the items referenced in these definitions. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>SEGMENT OPERATING INCOME </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company uses segment
operating income to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. The company believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze segment performance and trends. Segment operating income excludes unrealized gains and
losses on hedging activities (which are a component of cost of sales), general corporate expenses (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses), amortization of intangibles, gains and losses on divestitures and
acquisition-related costs (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses), in all periods presented. The company excludes these items from segment operating income in order to provide better transparency of its segment
operating results. Furthermore, the company centrally manages benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT> income and interest and other expense, net. Accordingly, the company does not present these items by segment because they
are excluded from the segment profitability measure that management reviews. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>ITEMS IMPACTING COMPARABILITY OF OPERATING RESULTS </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following information is provided to give qualitative and quantitative information related to items impacting comparability of operating results. The
company identifies these based on how management views the company&#146;s business; makes financial, operating and planning decisions; and evaluates the company&#146;s ongoing performance. In addition, the company discloses the impact of changes in
currency exchange rates on the company&#146;s financial results in order to reflect results on a constant currency basis. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Divestitures,
Divestiture-related costs and Gains/(losses) on divestitures </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Divestitures include completed sales of businesses and exits of major product lines
upon completion of a sale or licensing agreement. Divestitures that occurred in 2017 included the following: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">On December&nbsp;28, 2017, the company completed the sale of a confectionery business in Japan. The company
recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> loss of $1&nbsp;million. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

(&#147;Kraft Foods Group&#148;, now a part of Kraft Heinz Company (&#147;KHC&#148;)), Kraft Foods Group and the company each granted the other various licenses to use certain trademarks in connection with particular product categories in specified
jurisdictions. On August&nbsp;17, 2017, the company entered into two agreements with KHC to terminate the licenses of certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">KHC-owned</FONT> brands used in the company&#146;s grocery business within its Europe
region and to transfer to KHC inventory and certain other assets. On August&nbsp;17, 2017, the first transaction closed, and on October&nbsp;23, 2017, the second transaction closed. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">On July&nbsp;4, 2017, the company completed the sale of most of its grocery business in Australia and New Zealand
to Bega Cheese Limited. The company recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $247&nbsp;million Australian dollars ($187&nbsp;million as of July&nbsp;4, 2017) on the sale. In the fourth quarter of 2017, the company recorded
a final $3&nbsp;million inventory-related working capital adjustment, increasing the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain in 2017 to $190&nbsp;million. During the first none months of 2017, the company also incurred
divestiture-related costs of $2&nbsp;million and a foreign currency hedge loss of $3&nbsp;million in connection with this transaction. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">On April&nbsp;28, 2017, the company completed the sale of several manufacturing facilities in France and the sale
or license of several local confectionery brands. During the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2018, the company reversed $3&nbsp;million of accrued expenses no longer required. The company also incurred divestiture-related costs of $1&nbsp;million
in the three months and $22&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017. The company recorded a $3&nbsp;million loss on the sale during the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2017. Divestiture-related costs were recorded within cost
of sales and selling, general and administrative expenses. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Acquisitions and Acquisition-related costs </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On June&nbsp;7, 2018, the company acquired a U.S. premium biscuit company, Tate&#146;s Bake Shop, within its North America segment and extended its premium
biscuit offerings. On a constant currency basis, the purchase added incremental net revenues of $23&nbsp;million in the three months and $30&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2018. In addition, the company incurred
acquisition-related costs of $1&nbsp;million in the three months and $14&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2018. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Acquisition
integration costs </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within the company&#146;s AMEA segment, in connection with the acquisition of a biscuit operation in Vietnam in 2015, the
company recorded integration costs of $1&nbsp;million in the three months and $4&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2018 and $1&nbsp;million in the three months ended and $2&nbsp;million in the nine months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2017. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Simplify to Grow Program </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On September&nbsp;6, 2018, the company&#146;s Board of Directors approved an extension of the restructuring program through 2022, an increase of
$1.3&nbsp;billion in the program charges and an increase of $700&nbsp;million in capital expenditures. The current restructuring program, as increased and extended by these actions, is now called the Simplify to Grow Program. The primary objective
of the Simplify to Grow Program is to reduce the company&#146;s operating cost structure in both its supply chain and overhead costs. The program is intended primarily to cover severance as well as asset disposals and other manufacturing-related <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Restructuring costs </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recorded restructuring charges of $56&nbsp;million in the three months and $220&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2018 and
$113&nbsp;million in the three months and $418&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017 within asset impairment and exit costs or benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT> income. These charges were for <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> asset write-downs (including accelerated depreciation and asset impairments), severance and other related costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Implementation costs </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Implementation costs primarily
relate to reorganizing the company&#146;s operations and facilities in connection with its supply chain reinvention program and other identified productivity and cost saving initiatives. The costs include incremental expenses related to the closure
of facilities, costs to terminate certain contracts and the simplification of the company&#146;s information systems. The company recorded implementation costs of $83&nbsp;million in the three months and $215&nbsp;million in the nine months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2018 and $62&nbsp;million in the three months and $179&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Gain on
equity method investment transaction </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July&nbsp;9, 2018, Keurig Green Mountain, Inc. (&#147;Keurig&#148;) closed on its definitive merger
agreement with Dr Pepper Snapple Group, Inc., and formed Keurig Dr Pepper Inc. (&#147;KDP&#148;), a publicly traded company. Following the close of the transaction, the company&#146;s 24.2% investment in Keurig together with the company&#146;s
shareholder loan receivable became a 13.8% investment in KDP. During the third quarter of 2018, the company recorded a preliminary <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $757&nbsp;million reported as a gain on equity method
transaction and $184&nbsp;million of deferred tax expense reported in the provision for income taxes (or $573&nbsp;million <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> related to the change in the company&#146;s ownership interest while KDP
finalizes the valuation for the transaction. As the company continues to have significant influence, the company continues to account for its investment in KDP under the equity method, resulting in recognizing its share of KDP earnings within the
company&#146;s earnings and its share of KDP dividends within the company&#146;s cash flows. In connection with this transaction, the company changed its accounting principle to reflect its share of Keurig&#146;s historical and KDP&#146;s ongoing
earnings on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-quarter</FONT> lag basis while the company continues to record dividends when cash is received. The company determined a lag was preferable as it enables the company to continue to report its
quarterly and annual results on a timely basis and to record its share of KDP&#146;s ongoing results once KDP has publicly reported its results. This change in accounting principle was applied retrospectively to all periods. While the company&#146;s
operating income did not change, equity method investment net earnings, net earnings, and earnings per share have been adjusted to reflect the lag across all reported periods. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Equity method investee adjustments </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within
Adjusted EPS, the company&#146;s equity method investment net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its investees&#146; unusual or infrequent items, such as acquisition and divestiture-related costs and restructuring program costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and currency derivative contracts
</I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company excludes unrealized gains and losses <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(mark-to-market</FONT></FONT>
impacts) from outstanding commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures until such time that the related exposures impact its operating results. The company
recorded net unrealized losses on commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives of $120&nbsp;million in the three months and net unrealized gains of $173&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2018 and net unrealized
gains of $28&nbsp;million in the three months and net unrealized losses of $69&nbsp;million in the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2017. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Intangible assets gains and losses </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Impairment charges </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the company&#146;s 2018 annual
testing of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-amortizable</FONT> intangible assets, the company recorded $68&nbsp;million of impairment charges in the third quarter of 2018 related to five trademarks. The impairments arose due to lower than
expected product growth. The company recorded charges related to gum, chocolate, biscuits and candy trademarks of $45&nbsp;million in Europe, $14&nbsp;million in North America and $9&nbsp;million in AMEA. The impairment charges were recorded within
asset impairment and exit costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the company&#146;s 2017 annual testing of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-amortizable</FONT> intangible
assets, the company recorded $70&nbsp;million of impairment charges in the third quarter of 2017 related to five trademarks. The impairments arose due to lower than expected growth in part driven by decisions to redirect support from these
trademarks to other regional and global brands. The company recorded charges related to candy and gum trademarks of $52&nbsp;million in AMEA, $11&nbsp;million in Europe, $5&nbsp;million in Latin America and $2&nbsp;million in North America. In
addition, during the third quarter of 2017, the company recorded a $1&nbsp;million impairment related to a transaction. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the second quarter of
2017, the company recorded a $38&nbsp;million intangible asset impairment charge resulting from a category decline and lower than expected product growth related to a gum trademark in its North America segment. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Remeasurement of net monetary position </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the
second quarter of 2018, primarily based on published estimates which indicated that Argentina&#146;s three-year cumulative inflation rate exceeded 100%, the company concluded that Argentina became a highly inflationary economy for accounting
purposes. As of July&nbsp;1, 2018, the company began to apply highly inflationary accounting for its Argentinian subsidiaries and changed their functional currency from the Argentinian peso to the U.S. dollar. On July&nbsp;1, 2018, both monetary and
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-monetary</FONT> assets and liabilities denominated in Argentinian pesos were remeasured into U.S. dollars. As of each subsequent balance sheet date, Argentinian peso denominated monetary assets and liabilities
were remeasured into U.S. dollars using the exchange rate as of the balance sheet date, with remeasurement and other transaction gains and losses recorded in net earnings. During the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2018, the company recorded a
$13&nbsp;million remeasurement loss within selling, general and administrative expenses related to the devaluation of the Argentinian peso denominated net monetary assets during the quarter. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Incremental expenses related to the malware incident </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On June&nbsp;27, 2017, a global malware incident impacted the company&#146;s business. The malware affected a significant portion of the company&#146;s global
sales, distribution and financial networks. In the last four days of the second quarter and during the third quarter of 2017, the company executed business continuity and contingency plans to contain the impact, minimize damages and restore its
systems environment. To date, the company has not found, nor does the company expect to find, any instances of Company or personal data released externally. The company has also restored its main operating systems and processes and enhanced its
system security. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the second quarter of 2017, the company estimated that the malware incident had a negative impact of 2.3% on its net revenue growth
and 2.4% on its Organic Net Revenue growth. The company also incurred incremental expenses of $7&nbsp;million as a result of the incident. The company recognized the majority of delayed second quarter shipments in its third quarter 2017 results,
although the company permanently lost some revenue. On a 2017 full-year basis, the company estimated the loss of revenue had a negative impact of 0.4% on its net revenue and Organic Net Revenue growth. The company also incurred total incremental
expenses of $84&nbsp;million predominantly during the second half of 2017 as part of the recovery effort. The recovery from the incident was largely resolved by December&nbsp;31, 2017 and the company continued efforts to strengthen its security
measures and further mitigate cybersecurity risks. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Gain related to interest rate swaps </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recognized a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> loss of $1&nbsp;million in the three months and a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $10&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2018, within interest and other expense, net related to certain forward-starting interest rate swaps for which the planned timing of
the related forecasted debt was changed. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Loss on debt extinguishment </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;17, 2018, the company completed a cash tender offer and retired $570&nbsp;million of the long-term U.S. dollar debt. The company recorded a loss
on debt extinguishment of $140&nbsp;million within interest and other expense, net related to the amount the company paid to retire the debt in excess of its carrying value and from recognizing unamortized discounts, deferred financing and other
cash costs in earnings at the time of the debt extinguishment. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;12, 2017, the company discharged $488&nbsp;million of its 6.500% U.S.
dollar-denominated debt. The company paid $504&nbsp;million, representing principal as well as past and future interest accruals from February 2017 through the August 2017 maturity date. The company recorded an $11&nbsp;million loss on debt
extinguishment within interest expense. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Impact from resolution of tax matters </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">A tax indemnification matter related to the company&#146;s 2007 acquisition of the <I>LU</I> biscuit business was closed during the quarter ended June&nbsp;30,
2018. The closure had no impact on net earnings, however, it did result in a $15&nbsp;million tax benefit that was fully offset by an $11&nbsp;million expense in selling, general and administrative expenses and a $4&nbsp;million expense in interest
and other expense, net. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the first quarter of 2017, the Brazilian Supreme Court (the &#147;Court&#148;) ruled against the Brazilian tax authorities
in a leading case related to the computation of certain indirect <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(non-income)</FONT> taxes. The Court ruled that the indirect tax base should not include a value-added tax known as &#147;ICMS&#148;. By removing the
ICMS from the tax base, the Court effectively eliminated a &#147;tax on a tax.&#148; The company&#146;s Brazilian subsidiary had received an injunction against making payments for the &#147;tax on a tax&#148; in 2008 and since that time until
December 2016, the company had accrued for this portion of the tax each quarter in the event that the tax was reaffirmed by the Brazilian courts. On September&nbsp;30, 2017, based on legal advice and the publication of the Court&#146;s decision
related to this case, the company determined that the likelihood that the increased tax base would be reinstated and assessed against the company was remote. Accordingly, the company reversed its accrual of 667&nbsp;million Brazilian reais, or
$212&nbsp;million as of September&nbsp;30, 2017, of which, $153&nbsp;million was recorded within selling, general and administrative expenses and $59&nbsp;million was recorded within interest and other expense, net. The Brazilian tax authority may
appeal the Court&#146;s decision, seeking potential clarification or adjustment of the terms of enforcement. The company continues to monitor developments in this matter and currently does not expect a material future impact on its financial
statements. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the first quarter of 2017, the Spanish Supreme Court decided, in the company&#146;s favor, an ongoing transfer pricing case with the
Spanish tax authorities related to businesses Cadbury divested prior to the company&#146;s acquisition of Cadbury. As a result of the final ruling, during the first quarter of 2017, the company recorded a favorable earnings impact of
$46&nbsp;million in selling, general and administrative expenses and $12&nbsp;million in interest and other expense, net, for a total <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> impact of $58&nbsp;million due to the <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> reversal of Cadbury-related accrued liabilities related to this matter. The company recorded a total of $4 million of income over the third and fourth quarters of 2017 in connection with the restated bank
guarantee releases. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>CEO transition remuneration </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On November&nbsp;20, 2017, Dirk Van de Put succeeded Irene Rosenfeld as CEO of Mondel&#275;z International. In order to incent Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put to join the
company, the company provided him compensation to make him whole for incentive awards he forfeited or grants that were not made to him when he left his former employer. In connection with Irene Rosenfeld&#146;s retirement, the company made her
outstanding grants of performance share units for the 2016-2018 and 2017-2019 performance cycles eligible for continued vesting and paid $0.5&nbsp;million salary for her service as Chairman from January through March 2018. The company refers to
these elements of Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put&#146;s and Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld&#146;s compensation arrangements together as &#147;CEO transition remuneration.&#148; </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company is excluding amounts it expenses as CEO transition remuneration from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results because those
amounts are not part of the company&#146;s regular compensation program and are incremental to amounts the company would have incurred as ongoing CEO compensation. The company incurred CEO transition remuneration of $4&nbsp;million in the three
months and $18&nbsp;million in the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2018. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>U.S. tax reform discrete impacts </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On December&nbsp;22, 2017, the United States enacted tax reform legislation that included a broad range of business tax provisions, including but not limited
to a reduction in the U.S. federal tax rate from 35% to 21% as well as provisions that limit or eliminate various deductions or credits. The legislation also causes U.S. allocated expenses (e.g. interest and general administrative expense) to be
taxed and imposes a new tax on U.S. cross-border payments, Furthermore, the legislation includes a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> transition tax on accumulated foreign earnings and profits. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Certain impacts of the new legislation would have generally required accounting to be completed in the period of enactment, however in response to the
complexities of this new legislation, the SEC issued guidance to provide companies with relief. The SEC provided up to a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-year</FONT> window for companies to finalize the accounting for the impacts of this new
legislation and the company anticipates finalizing its accounting during 2018. While the company&#146;s accounting for the enactment of the new U.S. tax legislation is not complete, during the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2018, the company
has recorded an $8&nbsp;million U.S. tax reform discrete net tax benefit, consisting of a $3&nbsp;million increase in its transition tax liability and $5&nbsp;million of costs from other provisional tax reform updates. During the nine months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2018, the company recorded $95&nbsp;million in discrete net tax costs primarily comprised of an increase to its transition tax liability of $89&nbsp;million as a result of additional guidance issued by the U.S. Department of
Treasury, the Internal Revenue Service and various state taxing authorities, new state legislation enacted during the period and further refinement of various components of the underlying calculations. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Impact from pension participation changes </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
impact from pension participation changes represent the charges incurred when employee groups are withdrawn from multiemployer pension plans and other changes in employee group pension plan participation. The company excludes these charges from its <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results because those amounts do not reflect the company&#146;s ongoing pension obligations. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the second
quarter of 2018, the company implemented two aspects of its second revised last, best and final offer made to the Bakery, Confectionery, Tobacco and Grain Millers Union with respect to 7 of 8 expired collective bargaining agreements. Implementation
resulted in the company withdrawing from the Bakery and Confectionery Union and Industry International Pension Fund (the &#147;Fund&#148;) with respect to those employees covered by the 7 collective bargaining agreements. In connection with that
action, the company estimated a partial withdrawal liability of $567&nbsp;million and within its North America segment, the company recorded a discounted liability and charge of $408&nbsp;million, $305&nbsp;million net of tax, which represents its
best estimate of the partial withdrawal liability absent an assessment from the Fund. The company may receive an assessment in 2018 or later, and the ultimate withdrawal liability may change from the currently estimated amount. In addition, the
company records an immaterial amount of accreted interest each quarter on the long-term liability within interest and other expense, net. For the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2018, the company recorded $3&nbsp;million for accreted interest.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Constant currency </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Management evaluates the
operating performance of the company and its international subsidiaries on a constant currency basis. The company determines its constant currency operating results by dividing or multiplying, as appropriate, the current period local currency
operating results by the currency exchange rates used to translate the company&#146;s financial statements in the comparable prior-year period to determine what the current period U.S. dollar operating results would have been if the currency
exchange rate had not changed from the comparable prior-year period. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>OUTLOOK </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
company&#146;s outlook for 2018 Organic Net Revenue growth, Adjusted Operating Income margin, Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis and Free Cash Flow are <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures that exclude or
otherwise adjust for items impacting comparability of financial results such as the impact of changes in foreign currency exchange rates, restructuring activities, acquisitions and divestitures. The company is not able to reconcile its projected
Organic Net Revenue growth to its projected reported net revenue growth for the full-year 2018 because the company is unable to predict the impact of foreign exchange due to the unpredictability of future changes in foreign exchange rates, which
could be material as a significant portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the U.S. The company is not able to reconcile its projected Adjusted Operating Income margin and Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis to its
projected reported operating income margin and reported diluted EPS growth for the full-year 2018 because the company is unable to predict the timing of its restructuring program costs,
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative contracts and impacts from potential acquisitions or divestitures well as the impact
of foreign exchange due to the unpredictability of future changes in foreign exchange rates, which could be material as a significant portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the U.S. The company is not able to reconcile its projected
Free Cash Flow to its projected net cash from operating activities for the full-year 2018 because the company is unable to predict the timing and amount of capital expenditures impacting cash flow. Therefore, because of the uncertainty and
variability of the nature and amount of future adjustments, which could be significant, the company is unable to provide a reconciliation of these measures without unreasonable effort. </P>
